# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture guide for kubelet container manager, including resource manager interactions and platform variance.

## Scope

Focus on the kubelet container manager subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

The document has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

**Structure:**

1. **Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies** — defines what the subsystem does (resource enforcement, not scheduling or container launch), its upstream inputs (pod specs, cAdvisor topology, feature gates, CRI runtime), and downstream outputs (cgroup writes, CRI resource updates, device mount options, re-sync events).

2. **Key Components and Responsibility Split** — explains each of the eight major components (`containerManagerImpl`, `CgroupManager`, `QOSContainerManager`, `PodContainerManager`, `NodeContainerManager`, `InternalContainerLifecycle`, CPU/Memory/Topology managers, Device Manager, DRA Manager) with their concrete struct names and file locations.

3. **End-to-End Flow** — traces five concrete flows: startup sequence, pod admission (the topology manager hint-gather-merge-allocate cycle), container launch (how CPU/memory affinity gets written into the CRI `ContainerConfig`), pod cgroup lifecycle (create through destroy), and the device health update loop that drives pod re-syncs.

4. **Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs** — covers cgroup write failures with the retry goroutine, checkpoint corruption requiring a node drain, the 8-NUMA-node hard limit in the topology manager, the two-phase admission/allocation tradeoff, and cgroup v1 deprecation.

5. **Extension Points, Customisation Hooks, and Risks** — documents how to add CPU manager policies, topology manager policies/scopes, device plugins, and DRA drivers, with associated operational risks.

6. **Operational Implications** — addresses CPU reconciliation burst load, QoS cgroup update cost at scale, systemd D-Bus latency vs. cgroupfs, restart resilience, and the `klog.TODO()` / cgrou
... (truncated)

\t}\n785: \tlogger.V(10).Info(\"Found init PID namespace\", \"namespace\", initPidNs)\n786: \tprocessPidNs, err := os.Readlink(fmt.Sprintf(\"/proc/%d/ns/pid\", pid))\n787: \tif err != nil {\n788: err := isProcessRunningInHost(logger, pid); err != nil {\n796: \t\t// Err on the side of caution. Avoid moving the docker daemon unless we are able to identify its context.\n797: \t\treturn err\n798: \t} else if !runningInHost {\n799: \t\t// Process is running inside a container. Don't touch that.\n800: \t\tlogger.V(2).Info(\"PID is not running in the host namespace\", \"pid\", pid)\n801: \t\treturn nil\n802: \t}\n803: \n804: \tvar errs []error\n805: \tif manager != nil {\n806: \t\tcont, err := getContainer(logger, pid)\n807: \t\tif err != nil {\n808: \t\t\terrs = append(errs, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to find container of PID %d: %v\", pid, err))\n809: \t\t}\n810: \n811: {\n816: \t\t\tname = cgroups.Name\n817: \t\t}\n818: \n819: \t\tif cont != name {\n820: \t\t\terr = manager.Apply(pid)\n821: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n822: \t\t\t\terrs = append(errs, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to move PID %d (in %q) to %q: %v\", pid, cont, name, err))\n823: \t\t\t}\n824: \t\t}\n825: \t}\n826: \n827: \t// Also apply oom-score-adj to processes\n828: \toomAdjuster := oom.NewOOMAdjuster()\n829: \tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Attempting to apply oom_score_adj to process\", \"oomScoreAdj\", oomScoreAdj, \"pid\", pid)\n830: \tif err := oomAdjuster.ApplyOOMScoreAdj(pid, oomScoreAdj); err != nil {\n831: PID %d: %v\", oomScoreAdj, pid, err))\n833: \t}\n834: \treturn utilerrors.NewAggregate(errs)\n835: }\n836: \n837: // getContainer returns the cgroup associated with the specified pid.\n838: // It enforces a unified hierarchy for memory and cpu cgroups.\n839: // On systemd environments, it uses the name=systemd cgroup for the specified pid.\n840: func getContainer(logger klog.Logger, pid int) (string, error) {\n841: \tcgs, err := cgroups.ParseCgroupFile(fmt.Sprintf(\"/proc/%d/cgroup\", pid))\n842: \tif err != nil {\n843: \t\treturn \"\", err\n844: \t}\n845: \n846: \tif cgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode() {\n847: \t\tc, found := cgs[\"\"]\n848: \t\tif !found {\n849: \t\t\treturn \"\", cgroups.NewNotFoundError(\"unified\")\n850: \t\t}\n851: \t\treturn c, nil\n852: \t}\n853: \n854: \tcpu, found := cgs[\"cpu\"]\n855: \tif !found {\n856: \t\treturn \"\", cgroups.NewNotFoundError(\"cpu\")\n857: \t}\n858: \tmemory, found := cgs[\"memory\"]\n859: \tif !found {\n860: \t\treturn \"\", cgroups.NewNotFoundError(\"memory\")\n861: \t}\n862: \n863: \t// since we use this container for accounting, we need to ensure its a unified hierarchy.\n864: \tif cpu != memory {\n865: \t\treturn \"\", fmt.Errorf(\"cpu and memory cgroup hierarchy not unified.  cpu: %s, memory: %s\", cpu, memory)\n866: \t}\n867: \n868: \t// on systemd, every pid is in a unified cgroup hierarchy (name=systemd as seen in systemd-cgls)\n869: \t// cpu and memory accounting is off by default, users may choose to enable it per unit or globally.\n870: \t// users could enable CPU and memory accounting globally via /etc/systemd/system.conf (DefaultCPUAccounting=true DefaultMemoryAccounting=true).\n871: \t// users could also enable CPU and memory accounting per unit via CPUAccounting=true and MemoryAccounting=true\n872: \t// we only warn if accounting is not enabled for CPU or memory so as to not break local development flows where kubelet is launched in a terminal.\n873: \t// for example, the cgroup for the user session will be something like /user.slice/user-X.slice/session-X.scope, but the cpu and memory\n874: \t// cgroup will be the closest ancestor // getQoSMemoryRequests sums and returns the memory request of all pods for\\n206: // guaranteed and burstable qos classes.\\n207: func (m *qosContainerManagerImpl) getQoSMemoryRequests() \\t\\tlogger.V(2).Info(\\\"Allocatable memory reported as 0, might be in standalone mode, not setting QoS memory limits\\\")\\n248: \\t\\treturn\\n249: \\t}\\n250: \\n251: \\tfor qos, limits := range (qosMemoryRequests[v1.PodQOSBurstable] * percentReserve / 100)\\n258: \\tconfigs[v1.PodQOSBurstable].ResourceParameters.Memory = &burstableLimit\\n259: \\tconfigs[v1.PodQOSBestEffort].ResourceParameters.Memory = &bestEffortLimit\\n260: }\\n261: \\n262: // retrySetMemoryReserve checks for any QoS cgroups over the limit\\n263: // that was attempted to be set in the first Update() and adjusts\\n264: // their memory limit to the usage to prevent further growth.\\n265: func (m *qosContainerManagerImpl) retrySetMemoryReserve(logger klog.Logger, configs map[v1.PodQOSClass]*CgroupConfig, percentReserve int64) {\\n266: \\t// Unreclaimable memory usage may already exceeded the desired limit\\n267: \\t// Attempt to set the limit near the current usage to put pressure\\n268: \\t// on the cgroup and prevent further growth.\\n269: \\tfor qos, config := range configs {\\n270: \\t\\tusage, err := m.cgroupManager.MemoryUsage(config.Name)\\n271: \\t\\tif err != nil {\\n272: \\t\\t\\tlogger.V(2).Info(\\\"Failed to get resource stats\\\", \\\"err\\\", err)\\n273: \\t\\t\\treturn\\n274: \\t\\t}\\n275: \\n276: \\t\\t// Because there is no good way to determine of the original Update()\\n277: \\t\\t// on the memory resource was successful, we determine failure of the\\n278: \\t\\t// first attempt by checking if the usage is above the limit we attempt\\n279: \\t\\t// to set.  If it is, we assume the first attempt to set the limit failed\\n280: \\t\\t// and try again setting the limit to the usage.  Otherwise we leave\\n281: \\t\\t// the CgroupConfig as is.\\n282: \\t\\tif configs[qos].ResourceParameters.Memory != nil && usage > *configs[qos].ResourceParameters.Memory {\\n283: \\t\\t\\tconfigs[qos].ResourceParameters.Memory = &usage\\n284: \\t\\t}\\n285: \\t}\\n286: }\\n287: \\n288: // setMemoryQoS sums the memory requests of all pods in the Burstable class,\\n289: // and set the sum memory as the memory.min in the Unified field of CgroupConfig.\\n290: func (m *qosContainerManagerImpl) setMemoryQoS(logger klog.Logger, configs map[v1.PodQOSClass]*CgroupConfig) {\\n291: \\tqosMemoryRequests := m.getQoSMemoryRequests()\\n292: \\n293: \\t// Calculate the memory.min:\\n294: \\t// for burstable(/kubepods/burstable): sum of all burstable pods\\n295: \\t// for v.DeepCopy()\n256: \t\tif cm.NodeConfig.SystemReserved != nil {\n257: \t\t\tvalue.Sub(cm.NodeConfig.SystemReserved[k])\n258: \t\t}\n259: \t\tif cm.NodeConfig.KubeReserved != nil {\n260: {
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager: Subsystem Architecture Guide\n\n## 1. Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe container manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) is the kubelet subsystem responsible for translating Kubernetes resource semantics\u2014CPU requests, memory limits, QoS classes, device plugins, NUMA topology\u2014into concrete OS-level enforcement. On Linux this means writing cgroup parameters. On other platforms it provides stubs or minimal implementations. It does not schedule pods (that is the kube-scheduler's job) nor does it launch containers (that is the CRI runtime's job). Its mandate is strictly _resource boundary enforcement_ and _device/hardware allocation_.\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream inputs:**\n- Pod specs from the kubelet's pod manager (via `ActivePodsFunc`)\n- Node hardware topology from cAdvisor (`cadvisorapi.MachineInfo`)\n- Feature gates from `utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate`\n- CRI runtime service for reading current container state and updating container resources (`internalapi.RuntimeService`)\n- Kubernetes API client for DRA (Dynamic Resource Allocation) claim resolution\n\n**Downstream outputs:**\n- Cgroup filesystem writes (memory limits, CPU shares/quotas, cpuset affinity, pids limits, hugetlb limits)\n- `ContainerResources` updates sent to the CRI runtime via `UpdateContainerResources()`\n- `RunContainerOptions` returned to `kuberuntime` containing device mounts, environment variables, and CDI device names\n- A `resourceupdates.Update` channel consumed by the kubelet sync loop to re-sync pods whose device health changed\n\n**Key external dependencies:**\n- `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups` (runc libcontainer): the actual cgroup read/write operations\n- `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups/systemd`: systemd cgroup name conversion\n- cAdvisor for machine topology and filesystem capacity\n- The kubelet lifecycle package (`pkg/kubelet/lifecycle`) for the `PodAdmitHandler` interface\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `ContainerManager` Interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`)\n\nThe top-level interface through which the rest of kubelet interacts with this subsystem. It exposes:\n\n- **Lifecycle**: `Start()`, which initialises all sub-managers and begins background goroutines\n- **Node capacity**: `GetCapacity()`, `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()`, `GetNodeAllocatableAbsolute()`\n- **Cgroup hierarchy**: `NewPodContainerManager()`, `GetQOSContainersInfo()`, `UpdateQOSCgroups()`, `GetPodCgroupRoot()`\n- **Resource allocation gate**: `GetResources()` (returns runtime options for a container), `UpdatePluginResources()`, `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`\n- **DRA**: `PrepareDynamicResources()`, `UnprepareDynamicResources()`, `PodMightNeedToUnprepareResources()`\n- **PodResources API**: implements `CPUsProvider`, `DevicesProvider`, `MemoryProvider`, `DynamicResourcesProvider`\n- **Event stream**: `Updates()` returns a channel for device-health-driven pod re-syncs\n\n### 2.2 `containerManagerImpl` (Linux, `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nThe concrete Linux implementation. It aggregates every sub-manager:\n\n```\ncontainerManagerImpl\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cgroupManager         CgroupManager           (cgroup filesystem CRUD)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 qosContainerManager   QOSContainerManager      (top-level QoS cgroups)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 deviceManager         devicemanager.Manager    (device plugins)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager            cpumanager.Manager       (CPU affinity/pinning)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager         memorymanager.Manager    (NUMA memory affinity)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 topologyManager       topologymanager.Manager  (cross-resource NUMA coordination)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 draManager            *dra.Manager             (Dynamic Resource Allocation)\n```\n\nPlatform variants:\n- `container_manager_windows.go` (`//go:build windows`): limited implementation with device manager, CPU manager, and memory manager, but no cgroup hierarchy.\n- `container_manager_stub.go`: no-op implementation for tests and unsupported platforms.\n- `container_manager_unsupported.go`: compile-time stub for unsupported OS.\n\n### 2.3 `CgroupManager` Interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`)\n\nAbstracts all cgroup filesystem operations. Two concrete implementations:\n- `cgroupV1impl` (`cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`): uses runc libcontainer's v1 manager; validates against an allowlist of `cpu`, `cpuacct`, `cpuset`, `memory`, `systemd`, `pids`, `hugetlb`.\n- `cgroupV2impl` (`cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`): unified hierarchy using runc's cgroupv2 manager.\n\nBoth are selected at runtime by `NewCgroupManager()` which calls `cgroupManager.Version()` to record whether the host uses v1 or v2. The `NodeConfig.CgroupDriver` field selects between raw cgroupfs paths and systemd slice names.\n\n**Name conversion**: The internal `CgroupName` type (a `[]string`, e.g. `{\"kubepods\", \"burstable\", \"pod<uid>\"}`) is converted to systemd's nested slice naming (`/kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-pod<uid>.slice`) by `CgroupName.ToSystemd()` in `cgroup_manager_linux.go:81`.\n\n### 2.4 `QOSContainerManager` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nCreates and maintains the three-tier cgroup hierarchy under the `kubepods` root:\n\n```\n/kubepods\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 /kubepods/burstable\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 /kubepods/besteffort\n(Guaranteed pods land directly under /kubepods)\n```\n\nOn startup it creates or updates the `burstable` and `besteffort` cgroups. It then runs a background goroutine (`periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval = 1 minute`) calling `UpdateCgroups()`, which:\n1. Sums CPU requests across all Burstable pods \u2192 sets `cpu.shares` on the burstable cgroup\n2. Ensures BestEffort stays at the kernel minimum (2 shares)\n3. If `MemoryQoS` feature gate is on and cgroup v2 is in use, sets `memory.min` for memory protection\n4. If `QOSReserved` feature gate is on, computes memory limits by tier and calls `retrySetMemoryReserve()` if the initial write fails (because current usage exceeds the desired limit)\n\n### 2.5 `PodContainerManager` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`, implemented in `pod_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nManages the per-pod cgroup that sits beneath the QoS tier cgroup. Two implementations:\n\n- `podContainerManagerImpl` (when `CgroupsPerQOS = true`): creates `pod<uid>` cgroups under the appropriate QoS cgroup; enforces CPU CFS quota, memory limits, pids limits, and MemoryQoS `memory.min`/`memory.high`; handles cgroup cleanup by killing all processes then deleting the cgroup.\n- `podContainerManagerNoop` (when `CgroupsPerQOS = false`): all methods are no-ops; `Exists()` always returns true.\n\n`GetPodContainerName()` determines the pod's position in the hierarchy by calling `v1qos.GetPodQOS(pod)` and constructing a `CgroupName` whose parent is the appropriate QoS cgroup root.\n\n### 2.6 `NodeContainerManager` (functions in `node_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nHandles the `kubepods` cgroup itself (the \"node allocatable\" enforcement boundary). Key responsibilities:\n- `createNodeAllocatableCgroups()`: creates the `kubepods` root cgroup if missing\n- `enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()`: applies computed resource limits to `kubepods`; spawns a retry goroutine (sleeping 1 minute between attempts) if the first `cgroupManager.Update()` call fails\n- `enforceExistingCgroup()`: enforces user-specified `KubeReserved` and `SystemReserved` limits on their respective cgroups\n- `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()`: computes `systemReserved + kubeReserved + hardEvictionThresholds`\n- `GetNodeAllocatableAbsolute()`: computes `capacity - reservation`\n\n### 2.7 `InternalContainerLifecycle` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\nA narrow interface called by `kuberuntime` at specific container lifecycle points:\n\n- `PreCreateContainer()` (Linux only, `internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go`): injects CPU affinity (`cpuset.cpus`) from the CPU manager and NUMA memory affinity (`cpuset.mems`) from the memory manager directly into the CRI `ContainerConfig` before the container is created.\n- `PreStartContainer()`: registers the container with the CPU manager (`AddContainer`), memory manager (`AddContainer`), and topology manager (`AddContainer`).\n- `PostStopContainer()`: deregisters from the topology manager (`RemoveContainer`).\n\n### 2.8 CPU Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/`)\n\nManages exclusive CPU pinning for Guaranteed QoS containers with integer CPU requests. Two policies:\n\n- **None policy** (`policy_none.go`): no-op; all containers share the full CPU set.\n- **Static policy** (`policy_static.go`): maintains three CPU sets:\n  - `SHARED`: default pool for non-pinned containers\n  - `RESERVED`: ceil(systemReserved + kubeReserved CPUs), always in the shared pool, never exclusively allocatable\n  - `EXCLUSIVE`: per-container allocations for Guaranteed pods with integer CPU requests\n\n  On allocation it calls `takeByTopology()` in `cpu_assignment.go` to select CPUs preferring NUMA-local and SMT-aligned groupings. The selected CPUs are removed from SHARED and stored in the checkpoint state.\n\nState is persisted to `cpu_manager_state` checkpoint file in `KubeletRootDir`. On start, the manager reconciles its persisted state against running containers by calling `UpdateContainerResources()` on the CRI runtime to re-apply `cpuset.cpus` settings. The reconciliation loop runs every `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod`.\n\n### 2.9 Memory Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/`)\n\nManages NUMA-aware memory allocation with two policies:\n- **None**: no-op.\n- **Static**: tracks available memory per NUMA node from machine topology; assigns Guaranteed pods to specific NUMA nodes and sets `cpuset.mems` in the container's cgroup.\n\nLike the CPU manager it uses a file-backed checkpoint and reconciles on startup.\n\n### 2.10 Topology Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/`)\n\nA coordination layer that collects NUMA affinity _hints_ from all registered `HintProvider`s (CPU manager, memory manager, device manager) and produces a consensus optimal NUMA affinity before any allocation is committed.\n\n**Policies** (`policy_*.go`):\n- `none`: accepts all allocations\n- `best-effort`: prefers NUMA-aligned allocations but does not reject on mismatch\n- `restricted`: rejects pods that cannot be NUMA-aligned\n- `single-numa-node`: requires all resources to fit on a single NUMA node\n\n**Scopes** (`scope_container.go`, `scope_pod.go`):\n- Container scope: runs the hint-merge algorithm per container\n- Pod scope: runs it once across all containers in the pod\n\nThe topology manager acts as a `PodAdmitHandler` (registered at `kubelet.go:1059` via `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`). During pod admission it calls `Admit()` which triggers `GetTopologyHints()` on each hint provider, merges the results, and then calls `Allocate()` on each provider with the agreed affinity stored in its `Store`. Hard limit: `defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes = 8`; more NUMA nodes cause an error at manager construction time.\n\n### 2.11 Device Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/`)\n\nManages device plugin registrations and allocations. The `ManagerImpl`:\n- Runs a gRPC server that device plugin DaemonSets register against (via the plugin watcher)\n- Maintains sets of healthy and unhealthy devices reported by each plugin\n- Checkpoints allocations to `checkpoint/` under `KubeletRootDir` to survive kubelet restarts\n- Implements `HintProvider` so topology manager can factor device topology into NUMA alignment\n- Exposes a health update channel (`update chan resourceupdates.Update`); when a device changes health state it sends pod UIDs that need re-syncing\n\nThe device manager's `GetDeviceRunContainerOptions()` returns the mounts, environment variables, and CDI device IDs required by the container's allocated devices; this is called from `containerManagerImpl.GetResources()`.\n\n### 2.12 DRA Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/`)\n\nImplements Dynamic Resource Allocation (feature-gated by `DynamicResourceAllocation`). Communicates with DRA drivers (DaemonSets that register via the DRA plugin API) to `PrepareResources()` and `UnprepareResources()` for pods. On kubelet restart it may need to unprepare resources for pods that were never cleaned up, detectable via `PodMightNeedToUnprepareResources()`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Flow\n\n### 3.1 Startup Sequence\n\n`NewContainerManager()` in `container_manager_linux.go:207`:\n\n1. Calls `GetCgroupSubsystems()` to enumerate mounted cgroup controllers.\n2. Detects swap state; emits warnings if swap is on and `tmpfs noswap` is unsupported.\n3. Queries cAdvisor for `MachineInfo` (CPU topology, NUMA nodes, memory) and `pidlimit.Stats()`.\n4. Constructs `CgroupManager` (v1 or v2, cgroupfs or systemd driver).\n5. Validates `cgroupRoot` exists; appends `defaultNodeAllocatableCgroupName` (`kubepods`) to get the actual pod root.\n6. Creates `QOSContainerManager`.\n7. Creates `topologymanager.Manager`.\n8. Creates `devicemanager.ManagerImpl`; registers it as a topology hint provider.\n9. Optionally creates `dra.Manager`; registers DRA metrics collector.\n10. Creates `cpumanager.Manager`; registers it as a topology hint provider.\n11. Creates `memorymanager.Manager`; registers it as a topology hint provider.\n12. Starts fan-in goroutines to multiplex update channels from device manager and DRA manager into a single `resourceUpdates` channel.\n\n`ContainerManager.Start()` in `container_manager_linux.go:615`:\n\n1. Builds `containerMap` from the CRI runtime to identify pre-existing containers.\n2. Starts DRA manager.\n3. Starts CPU manager (loads checkpoint, reconciles existing containers, starts reconcile loop).\n4. Starts memory manager (same pattern).\n5. Caches node info; fetches rootfs capacity from cAdvisor if local storage isolation is on.\n6. Validates node allocatable configuration.\n7. Calls `setupNode()`:\n   a. Validates required cgroup subsystems exist (`validateSystemRequirements()`).\n   b. Sets kernel tunables (`vm.overcommit_memory`, `vm.panic_on_oom`, `kernel.panic`, `kernel.panic_on_oops`, keyring limits) based on `ProtectKernelDefaults`.\n   c. Creates and starts QOS container hierarchy if `CgroupsPerQOS`.\n   d. Enforces node allocatable cgroups.\n   e. Sets up `systemContainers` for the runtime and kubelet itself.\n8. Starts periodic goroutines for `ensureStateFunc` (every 1 minute) and any periodic tasks (every 5 minutes).\n9. Starts device manager (begins serving device plugin gRPC, loads checkpoints, reconciles containers).\n\n### 3.2 Pod Admission Flow\n\nWhen a new pod arrives and passes through kubelet's admit handlers (`kubelet.go:1059`):\n\n```\nlifecycle.PodAdmitHandler chain\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 containerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 topologymanager.Manager.Admit()\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 For each container in pod:\n        \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.GetTopologyHints()\n        \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.GetTopologyHints()\n        \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.GetTopologyHints()\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Merge hints \u2192 best NUMA affinity bitmask\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 For each container:\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.Allocate()    \u2192 reserves CPUs in state\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.Allocate() \u2192 reserves NUMA memory blocks\n            \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.Allocate() \u2192 calls device plugin Allocate RPC\n```\n\nAdditionally `lifecycle.NewPredicateAdmitHandler` calls `containerManager.UpdatePluginResources()`, which delegates to the device manager to update the scheduler's node info with current allocatable device capacity.\n\n### 3.3 Container Launch Flow\n\nWhen `kuberuntime` creates a container it calls through `InternalContainerLifecycle`:\n\n```\nkuberuntime.createContainer()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 internalContainerLifecycle.PreCreateContainer()\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity() \u2192 inject cpuset.cpus into ContainerConfig\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.GetMemoryNUMANodes() \u2192 inject cpuset.mems into ContainerConfig\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 containerManager.GetResources()\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 draManager.GetResources() \u2192 CDI device IDs for DRA\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions() \u2192 mounts, env vars, CDI devices\n\u2502       (allocation was already done at admission; this reads cached state)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 CRI: CreateContainer(ContainerConfig with cpuset.cpus, cpuset.mems, devices, mounts)\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 internalContainerLifecycle.PreStartContainer()\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.AddContainer() \u2192 records containerID \u2192 (pod, container) mapping\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.AddContainer() \u2192 same\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 topologyManager.AddContainer() \u2192 tracks for hint store\n```\n\n### 3.4 Pod Cgroup Lifecycle\n\nPod workers call `PodContainerManager.EnsureExists()` before running any containers:\n\n```\npodContainerManagerImpl.EnsureExists()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Determine QoS class \u2192 parent cgroup path\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Build ResourceConfig from pod spec:\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 ResourceConfigForPod() \u2192 CPU shares, CFS quota, memory limit\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 PidsLimit if configured\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 MemoryQoS unified fields (memory.min, memory.high) if cgroup v2 + feature gate\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 cgroupManager.Create()\n```\n\nOn pod termination, pod workers call `PodContainerManager.Destroy()`:\n\n```\npodContainerManagerImpl.Destroy()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 tryKillingCgroupProcesses() \u2192 kill all PIDs in cgroup (up to 5 retries)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 cgroupManager.Destroy()    \u2192 rmdir the cgroup\n```\n\n### 3.5 Device Health Update Loop\n\nWhen a device plugin reports a device health change, the device manager sends to its internal `update` channel. A fan-in goroutine in `NewContainerManager` (`container_manager_linux.go:375`) forwards this to `cm.resourceUpdates`. The kubelet sync loop reads from `containerManager.Updates()` (`kubelet.go:2665`) and calls `handler.HandlePodSyncs()` for affected pods, causing a fresh status update that reflects the new device health.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n**Cgroup write failures on node allocatable enforcement**: `enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()` (`node_container_manager_linux.go:95`) spawns a background goroutine that retries `cgroupManager.Update()` indefinitely with 1-minute sleeps, emitting Kubernetes Warning events on each failure. This prevents a hard startup failure when existing pod memory usage temporarily exceeds the new limit.\n\n**QoS cgroup update failures**: `qosContainerManagerImpl.UpdateCgroups()` (`qos_container_manager_linux.go:316`) attempts a `retrySetMemoryReserve()` fallback that caps the limit to current memory usage when the first write is rejected. If updates still fail, the error is logged but the goroutine continues; QoS limits may drift from desired state until the next 1-minute reconcile.\n\n**CPU manager checkpoint corruption**: If `state.NewCheckpointState()` fails, the CPU manager refuses to start and the kubelet returns an error. The operator must drain the node and remove the state file. This is intentional\u2014silently starting with corrupt state would produce incorrect CPU pinning.\n\n**Device plugin crashes**: The device manager marks devices from a crashed plugin as unhealthy and sends updates via the health channel. Pods using those devices get re-synced; the kubelet emits events. The checkpoint retains allocations so that if the plugin reconnects before the pod is deleted, allocation state can be reconciled.\n\n**NUMA nodes > 8**: `topology_manager.go:41` defines `defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes = 8`. Exceeding this causes `topologymanager.NewManager()` to return an error, preventing kubelet startup with topology manager enabled on large multi-socket machines.\n\n**Swap enabled with `failSwapOn=true`**: `NewContainerManager` returns an error immediately, preventing kubelet from starting. With `failSwapOn=false`, the kubelet continues but emits a warning event about memory-backed volumes potentially being swapped to disk.\n\n**cgroup v1 on new kernels**: A deprecation warning (`CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning`) is defined in `container_manager.go:52`. cgroup v1 support is intended for removal in a future release.\n\n### 4.2 Design Tradeoffs\n\n**Two-phase admission/allocation**: The topology manager's `Admit()` phase calls `Allocate()` on hint providers before the container is created. This means device allocations are committed at pod admission time, not at container start time. If the container never starts (e.g., image pull failure), the device remains allocated until the kubelet cleans up the pod.\n\n**Checkpoint-based state persistence**: CPU, memory, and device managers all use checkpoint files under `KubeletRootDir`. This allows kubelet restarts without losing allocations. The downside is that checkpoint format changes require migration logic and draining.\n\n**Synchronous QoS hierarchy updates**: The QoS cgroup update goroutine holds a mutex for its entire update cycle. During that time, new pod admissions that need `UpdateQOSCgroups()` must wait. This is acceptable because the update is fast (a few cgroup writes) and happens only once per minute.\n\n**Noop implementations as a compile-time seam**: The `containerManagerStub` (`container_manager_stub.go`) and `podContainerManagerNoop` provide full no-op implementations of the interfaces. This decouples the kubelet's main path from the Linux-specific cgroup machinery at the cost of maintaining two parallel code paths.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customisation Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policy\n\n`cpumanager.Policy` is an interface (`policy.go`) with `Start()`, `Allocate()`, `RemoveContainer()`, `GetTopologyHints()`, `GetAllocatableCPUs()`. New policies can be registered by adding a `case` to the `switch` in `NewManager()`. Policy options (`CPUManagerPolicyOptions map[string]string` in `NodeConfig`) allow feature flags per policy without changing the interface.\n\nThe static policy has options including `full-pcpus-only` (require whole physical cores), `distribute-cpus-across-numa`, `distribute-cpus-across-cores`, and `align-by-socket`. These are parsed in `policy_options.go` and change the CPU assignment topology.\n\n**Risk**: A buggy policy can silently mis-assign CPUs or fail to clean up exclusive allocations; the CPU set leaked from a terminated container remains unavailable for new ones until the reconciler detects the container is gone.\n\n### 5.2 Topology Manager Policy and Scope\n\nBoth `TopologyManagerPolicy` and `TopologyManagerScope` are strings from `NodeConfig`. Adding a new policy requires adding a `policy_*.go` file and registering it in `topology_manager.go`. The scope (container vs. pod) changes whether hints are merged per-container or across all containers at once.\n\n**Risk**: `best-effort` silently allows non-optimal NUMA placement; operators may not notice increased cross-NUMA memory traffic until they measure latency. `restricted` and `single-numa-node` can cause admission failures that are opaque to end users if hint providers cannot agree.\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugins\n\nDevice plugins register via the plugin watcher (`GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` returns a map including `DevicePlugin` \u2192 `deviceManager.GetWatcherHandler()`). Any DaemonSet can register additional resource types without modifying kubelet code. The device manager's `Allocate()` delegates entirely to the plugin's gRPC response.\n\n**Risk**: A device plugin that returns inconsistent topology information will cause the topology manager to make suboptimal NUMA placements. A plugin that crashes at `Allocate()` time causes pod admission to fail; kubelet will retry the admission on the next sync cycle.\n\n### 5.4 DRA Drivers\n\nDRA drivers register via the DRA plugin watcher (`DRAPlugin` key in `GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()`). The `dra.Manager` communicates with the driver to `PrepareResources()`, writing CDI device annotations that are passed to the CRI runtime. DRA is gated by `DynamicResourceAllocation` feature gate.\n\n**Risk**: DRA state is stored in `ResourceClaim` objects in the API server and locally in the DRA manager's state directory. Inconsistencies between these two sources of truth on kubelet restart require the `PodMightNeedToUnprepareResources()` / `UnprepareResources()` recovery path; if the driver itself is unavailable at unprepare time, resources may leak.\n\n### 5.5 MemoryQoS (cgroup v2 only)\n\nControlled by the `MemoryQoS` feature gate. When enabled, `memory.min` is set on QoS cgroups and pod cgroups to provide memory protection guarantees. The `Unified` map field in `ResourceConfig` carries arbitrary cgroup v2 key-value pairs, providing an extension point for future cgroup v2 features without changing the `ResourceConfig` struct.\n\n### 5.6 PodLevelResources\n\nThe `qos_container_manager_linux.go:188` references `kubefeatures.PodLevelResources` to decide whether to skip pod-level resource aggregation when computing Burstable CPU shares. This is an example of a feature gate that changes the aggregation semantics within an existing component.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance\n\n**CPU manager reconciliation**: The reconcile loop calls `UpdateContainerResources()` on the CRI runtime for every container whose CPU set has changed since the last reconcile. On a node with hundreds of containers and the static policy, this can produce bursts of gRPC calls. The reconcile period (`CPUManagerReconcilePeriod`, default 10 seconds) controls this tradeoff.\n\n**QoS cgroup update cost**: Every minute, `UpdateCgroups()` iterates all active pods to sum CPU requests. On nodes with many pods, this is O(pods \u00d7 containers). The update itself is a handful of cgroup writes, but the pod iteration under lock can delay admission.\n\n**Cgroup write latency on systemd**: When using the systemd cgroup driver, `cgroup_manager_linux.go` converts every cgroup name to a systemd slice path. Systemd must be notified via D-Bus for each cgroup operation. On high-density nodes this can become a bottleneck; the cgroupfs driver avoids this overhead.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\n**Kubelet restart resilience**: CPU, memory, and device managers write state to checkpoint files before returning success from `Allocate()`. On restart, `Start()` reads the checkpoint and calls `UpdateContainerResources()` for any container still running to restore affinity. This means brief affinity drift (the container runs on the wrong CPUs) during the window between kubelet crash and restart recovery.\n\n**cgroup hierarchy divergence**: The QoS and pod container managers are responsible for creating and destroying cgroups in sync with pod lifecycle. If the kubelet crashes between creating a pod cgroup and launching the container, orphan cgroups may exist. `GetAllPodsFromCgroups()` on `podContainerManagerImpl` scans the filesystem to enumerate orphan pod cgroups, which `HandlePodCleanups()` uses for garbage collection.\n\n**`ShouldResetExtendedResourceCapacity()`**: Called on kubelet startup via `kubelet_resources.go`. The device manager returns `true` if the checkpoint indicates the node identity changed (e.g., node was recreated). In that case the kubelet zeroes extended resource capacity in the node status, forcing device plugins to re-register.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\n**cgroup v1 deprecation**: `container_manager.go:52` contains the deprecation warning. The v1-specific code paths in `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` and the v1 branches in `helpers_linux.go` represent ongoing maintenance burden. Removal requires coordinated changes across multiple files.\n\n**`klog.TODO()` debt**: Several methods in `container_manager_linux.go` (e.g., `PodHasExclusiveCPUs`, `GetCapacity`) call `klog.TODO()` because they lack a proper context. This is flagged in source comments as a known issue requiring refactoring to pass loggers through more of the call chain.\n\n**Mockery-generated mocks**: The `//go:generate mockery` directive in `container_manager.go` generates mocks for testing. The `.mockery.yaml` controls which interfaces are mocked. This keeps test doubles in sync with the interface, but any interface change requires running `go generate` and committing updated mock files.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` | `ContainerManager` interface, `NodeConfig`, `NodeAllocatableConfig`, helper functions |\n| {
  "content": "# Kubelet Container Manager: Subsystem Architecture Guide\n\n## 1. Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe container manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) is the kubelet subsystem responsible for translating Kubernetes resource semantics\u2014CPU requests, memory limits, QoS classes, device plugins, NUMA topology\u2014into concrete OS-level enforcement. On Linux this means writing cgroup parameters. On other platforms it provides stubs or minimal implementations. It does not schedule pods (that is the kube-scheduler's job) nor does it launch containers (that is the CRI runtime's job). Its mandate is strictly _resource boundary enforcement_ and _device/hardware allocation_.\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream inputs:**\n- Pod specs from the kubelet's pod manager (via `ActivePodsFunc`)\n- Node hardware topology from cAdvisor (`cadvisorapi.MachineInfo`)\n- Feature gates from `utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate`\n- CRI runtime service for reading current container state and updating container resources (`internalapi.RuntimeService`)\n- Kubernetes API client for DRA (Dynamic Resource Allocation) claim resolution\n\n**Downstream outputs:**\n- Cgroup filesystem writes (memory limits, CPU shares/quotas, cpuset affinity, pids limits, hugetlb limits)\n- `ContainerResources` updates sent to the CRI runtime via `UpdateContainerResources()`\n- `RunContainerOptions` returned to `kuberuntime` containing device mounts, environment variables, and CDI device names\n- A `resourceupdates.Update` channel consumed by the kubelet sync loop to re-sync pods whose device health changed\n\n**Key external dependencies:**\n- `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups` (runc libcontainer): the actual cgroup read/write operations\n- `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups/systemd`: systemd cgroup name conversion\n- cAdvisor for machine topology and filesystem capacity\n- The kubelet lifecycle package (`pkg/kubelet/lifecycle`) for the `PodAdmitHandler` interface\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `ContainerManager` Interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go`)\n\nThe top-level interface through which the rest of kubelet interacts with this subsystem. It exposes:\n\n- **Lifecycle**: `Start()`, which initialises all sub-managers and begins background goroutines\n- **Node capacity**: `GetCapacity()`, `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()`, `GetNodeAllocatableAbsolute()`\n- **Cgroup hierarchy**: `NewPodContainerManager()`, `GetQOSContainersInfo()`, `UpdateQOSCgroups()`, `GetPodCgroupRoot()`\n- **Resource allocation gate**: `GetResources()` (returns runtime options for a container), `UpdatePluginResources()`, `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`\n- **DRA**: `PrepareDynamicResources()`, `UnprepareDynamicResources()`, `PodMightNeedToUnprepareResources()`\n- **PodResources API**: implements `CPUsProvider`, `DevicesProvider`, `MemoryProvider`, `DynamicResourcesProvider`\n- **Event stream**: `Updates()` returns a channel for device-health-driven pod re-syncs\n\n### 2.2 `containerManagerImpl` (Linux, `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nThe concrete Linux implementation. It aggregates every sub-manager:\n\n```\ncontainerManagerImpl\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cgroupManager         CgroupManager           (cgroup filesystem CRUD)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 qosContainerManager   QOSContainerManager      (top-level QoS cgroups)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 deviceManager         devicemanager.Manager    (device plugins)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager            cpumanager.Manager       (CPU affinity/pinning)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager         memorymanager.Manager    (NUMA memory affinity)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 topologyManager       topologymanager.Manager  (cross-resource NUMA coordination)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 draManager            *dra.Manager             (Dynamic Resource Allocation)\n```\n\nPlatform variants:\n- `container_manager_windows.go` (`//go:build windows`): limited implementation with device manager, CPU manager, and memory manager, but no cgroup hierarchy.\n- `container_manager_stub.go`: no-op implementation for tests and unsupported platforms.\n- `container_manager_unsupported.go`: compile-time stub for unsupported OS.\n\n### 2.3 `CgroupManager` Interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`)\n\nAbstracts all cgroup filesystem operations. Two concrete implementations:\n- `cgroupV1impl` (`cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`): uses runc libcontainer's v1 manager; validates against an allowlist of `cpu`, `cpuacct`, `cpuset`, `memory`, `systemd`, `pids`, `hugetlb`.\n- `cgroupV2impl` (`cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`): unified hierarchy using runc's cgroupv2 manager.\n\nBoth are selected at runtime by `NewCgroupManager()` which calls `cgroupManager.Version()` to record whether the host uses v1 or v2. The `NodeConfig.CgroupDriver` field selects between raw cgroupfs paths and systemd slice names.\n\n**Name conversion**: The internal `CgroupName` type (a `[]string`, e.g. `{\"kubepods\", \"burstable\", \"pod<uid>\"}`) is converted to systemd's nested slice naming (`/kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-pod<uid>.slice`) by `CgroupName.ToSystemd()` in `cgroup_manager_linux.go:81`.\n\n### 2.4 `QOSContainerManager` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nCreates and maintains the three-tier cgroup hierarchy under the `kubepods` root:\n\n```\n/kubepods\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 /kubepods/burstable\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 /kubepods/besteffort\n(Guaranteed pods land directly under /kubepods)\n```\n\nOn startup it creates or updates the `burstable` and `besteffort` cgroups. It then runs a background goroutine (`periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval = 1 minute`) calling `UpdateCgroups()`, which:\n1. Sums CPU requests across all Burstable pods \u2192 sets `cpu.shares` on the burstable cgroup\n2. Ensures BestEffort stays at the kernel minimum (2 shares)\n3. If `MemoryQoS` feature gate is on and cgroup v2 is in use, sets `memory.min` for memory protection\n4. If `QOSReserved` feature gate is on, computes memory limits by tier and calls `retrySetMemoryReserve()` if the initial write fails (because current usage exceeds the desired limit)\n\n### 2.5 `PodContainerManager` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go`, implemented in `pod_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nManages the per-pod cgroup that sits beneath the QoS tier cgroup. Two implementations:\n\n- `podContainerManagerImpl` (when `CgroupsPerQOS = true`): creates `pod<uid>` cgroups under the appropriate QoS cgroup; enforces CPU CFS quota, memory limits, pids limits, and MemoryQoS `memory.min`/`memory.high`; handles cgroup cleanup by killing all processes then deleting the cgroup.\n- `podContainerManagerNoop` (when `CgroupsPerQOS = false`): all methods are no-ops; `Exists()` always returns true.\n\n`GetPodContainerName()` determines the pod's position in the hierarchy by calling `v1qos.GetPodQOS(pod)` and constructing a `CgroupName` whose parent is the appropriate QoS cgroup root.\n\n### 2.6 `NodeContainerManager` (functions in `node_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\nHandles the `kubepods` cgroup itself (the \"node allocatable\" enforcement boundary). Key responsibilities:\n- `createNodeAllocatableCgroups()`: creates the `kubepods` root cgroup if missing\n- `enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()`: applies computed resource limits to `kubepods`; spawns a retry goroutine (sleeping 1 minute between attempts) if the first `cgroupManager.Update()` call fails\n- `enforceExistingCgroup()`: enforces user-specified `KubeReserved` and `SystemReserved` limits on their respective cgroups\n- `GetNodeAllocatableReservation()`: computes `systemReserved + kubeReserved + hardEvictionThresholds`\n- `GetNodeAllocatableAbsolute()`: computes `capacity - reservation`\n\n### 2.7 `InternalContainerLifecycle` (`pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\nA narrow interface called by `kuberuntime` at specific container lifecycle points:\n\n- `PreCreateContainer()` (Linux only, `internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go`): injects CPU affinity (`cpuset.cpus`) from the CPU manager and NUMA memory affinity (`cpuset.mems`) from the memory manager directly into the CRI `ContainerConfig` before the container is created.\n- `PreStartContainer()`: registers the container with the CPU manager (`AddContainer`), memory manager (`AddContainer`), and topology manager (`AddContainer`).\n- `PostStopContainer()`: deregisters from the topology manager (`RemoveContainer`).\n\n### 2.8 CPU Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/`)\n\nManages exclusive CPU pinning for Guaranteed QoS containers with integer CPU requests. Two policies:\n\n- **None policy** (`policy_none.go`): no-op; all containers share the full CPU set.\n- **Static policy** (`policy_static.go`): maintains three CPU sets:\n  - `SHARED`: default pool for non-pinned containers\n  - `RESERVED`: ceil(systemReserved + kubeReserved CPUs), always in the shared pool, never exclusively allocatable\n  - `EXCLUSIVE`: per-container allocations for Guaranteed pods with integer CPU requests\n\n  On allocation it calls `takeByTopology()` in `cpu_assignment.go` to select CPUs preferring NUMA-local and SMT-aligned groupings. The selected CPUs are removed from SHARED and stored in the checkpoint state.\n\nState is persisted to `cpu_manager_state` checkpoint file in `KubeletRootDir`. On start, the manager reconciles its persisted state against running containers by calling `UpdateContainerResources()` on the CRI runtime to re-apply `cpuset.cpus` settings. The reconciliation loop runs every `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod`.\n\n### 2.9 Memory Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/`)\n\nManages NUMA-aware memory allocation with two policies:\n- **None**: no-op.\n- **Static**: tracks available memory per NUMA node from machine topology; assigns Guaranteed pods to specific NUMA nodes and sets `cpuset.mems` in the container's cgroup.\n\nLike the CPU manager it uses a file-backed checkpoint and reconciles on startup.\n\n### 2.10 Topology Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/`)\n\nA coordination layer that collects NUMA affinity _hints_ from all registered `HintProvider`s (CPU manager, memory manager, device manager) and produces a consensus optimal NUMA affinity before any allocation is committed.\n\n**Policies** (`policy_*.go`):\n- `none`: accepts all allocations\n- `best-effort`: prefers NUMA-aligned allocations but does not reject on mismatch\n- `restricted`: rejects pods that cannot be NUMA-aligned\n- `single-numa-node`: requires all resources to fit on a single NUMA node\n\n**Scopes** (`scope_container.go`, `scope_pod.go`):\n- Container scope: runs the hint-merge algorithm per container\n- Pod scope: runs it once across all containers in the pod\n\nThe topology manager acts as a `PodAdmitHandler` (registered at `kubelet.go:1059` via `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`). During pod admission it calls `Admit()` which triggers `GetTopologyHints()` on each hint provider, merges the results, and then calls `Allocate()` on each provider with the agreed affinity stored in its `Store`. Hard limit: `defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes = 8`; more NUMA nodes cause an error at manager construction time.\n\n### 2.11 Device Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/`)\n\nManages device plugin registrations and allocations. The `ManagerImpl`:\n- Runs a gRPC server that device plugin DaemonSets register against (via the plugin watcher)\n- Maintains sets of healthy and unhealthy devices reported by each plugin\n- Checkpoints allocations to `checkpoint/` under `KubeletRootDir` to survive kubelet restarts\n- Implements `HintProvider` so topology manager can factor device topology into NUMA alignment\n- Exposes a health update channel (`update chan resourceupdates.Update`); when a device changes health state it sends pod UIDs that need re-syncing\n\nThe device manager's `GetDeviceRunContainerOptions()` returns the mounts, environment variables, and CDI device IDs required by the container's allocated devices; this is called from `containerManagerImpl.GetResources()`.\n\n### 2.12 DRA Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/`)\n\nImplements Dynamic Resource Allocation (feature-gated by `DynamicResourceAllocation`). Communicates with DRA drivers (DaemonSets that register via the DRA plugin API) to `PrepareResources()` and `UnprepareResources()` for pods. On kubelet restart it may need to unprepare resources for pods that were never cleaned up, detectable via `PodMightNeedToUnprepareResources()`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Flow\n\n### 3.1 Startup Sequence\n\n`NewContainerManager()` in `container_manager_linux.go:207`:\n\n1. Calls `GetCgroupSubsystems()` to enumerate mounted cgroup controllers.\n2. Detects swap state; emits warnings if swap is on and `tmpfs noswap` is unsupported.\n3. Queries cAdvisor for `MachineInfo` (CPU topology, NUMA nodes, memory) and `pidlimit.Stats()`.\n4. Constructs `CgroupManager` (v1 or v2, cgroupfs or systemd driver).\n5. Validates `cgroupRoot` exists; appends `defaultNodeAllocatableCgroupName` (`kubepods`) to get the actual pod root.\n6. Creates `QOSContainerManager`.\n7. Creates `topologymanager.Manager`.\n8. Creates `devicemanager.ManagerImpl`; registers it as a topology hint provider.\n9. Optionally creates `dra.Manager`; registers DRA metrics collector.\n10. Creates `cpumanager.Manager`; registers it as a topology hint provider.\n11. Creates `memorymanager.Manager`; registers it as a topology hint provider.\n12. Starts fan-in goroutines to multiplex update channels from device manager and DRA manager into a single `resourceUpdates` channel.\n\n`ContainerManager.Start()` in `container_manager_linux.go:615`:\n\n1. Builds `containerMap` from the CRI runtime to identify pre-existing containers.\n2. Starts DRA manager.\n3. Starts CPU manager (loads checkpoint, reconciles existing containers, starts reconcile loop).\n4. Starts memory manager (same pattern).\n5. Caches node info; fetches rootfs capacity from cAdvisor if local storage isolation is on.\n6. Validates node allocatable configuration.\n7. Calls `setupNode()`:\n   a. Validates required cgroup subsystems exist (`validateSystemRequirements()`).\n   b. Sets kernel tunables (`vm.overcommit_memory`, `vm.panic_on_oom`, `kernel.panic`, `kernel.panic_on_oops`, keyring limits) based on `ProtectKernelDefaults`.\n   c. Creates and starts QOS container hierarchy if `CgroupsPerQOS`.\n   d. Enforces node allocatable cgroups.\n   e. Sets up `systemContainers` for the runtime and kubelet itself.\n8. Starts periodic goroutines for `ensureStateFunc` (every 1 minute) and any periodic tasks (every 5 minutes).\n9. Starts device manager (begins serving device plugin gRPC, loads checkpoints, reconciles containers).\n\n### 3.2 Pod Admission Flow\n\nWhen a new pod arrives and passes through kubelet's admit handlers (`kubelet.go:1059`):\n\n```\nlifecycle.PodAdmitHandler chain\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 containerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 topologymanager.Manager.Admit()\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 For each container in pod:\n        \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.GetTopologyHints()\n        \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.GetTopologyHints()\n        \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.GetTopologyHints()\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 Merge hints \u2192 best NUMA affinity bitmask\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 For each container:\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.Allocate()    \u2192 reserves CPUs in state\n            \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.Allocate() \u2192 reserves NUMA memory blocks\n            \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.Allocate() \u2192 calls device plugin Allocate RPC\n```\n\nAdditionally `lifecycle.NewPredicateAdmitHandler` calls `containerManager.UpdatePluginResources()`, which delegates to the device manager to update the scheduler's node info with current allocatable device capacity.\n\n### 3.3 Container Launch Flow\n\nWhen `kuberuntime` creates a container it calls through `InternalContainerLifecycle`:\n\n```\nkuberuntime.createContainer()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 internalContainerLifecycle.PreCreateContainer()\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity() \u2192 inject cpuset.cpus into ContainerConfig\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.GetMemoryNUMANodes() \u2192 inject cpuset.mems into ContainerConfig\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 containerManager.GetResources()\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 draManager.GetResources() \u2192 CDI device IDs for DRA\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 deviceManager.GetDeviceRunContainerOptions() \u2192 mounts, env vars, CDI devices\n\u2502       (allocation was already done at admission; this reads cached state)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 CRI: CreateContainer(ContainerConfig with cpuset.cpus, cpuset.mems, devices, mounts)\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 internalContainerLifecycle.PreStartContainer()\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 cpuManager.AddContainer() \u2192 records containerID \u2192 (pod, container) mapping\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 memoryManager.AddContainer() \u2192 same\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 topologyManager.AddContainer() \u2192 tracks for hint store\n```\n\n### 3.4 Pod Cgroup Lifecycle\n\nPod workers call `PodContainerManager.EnsureExists()` before running any containers:\n\n```\npodContainerManagerImpl.EnsureExists()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Determine QoS class \u2192 parent cgroup path\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Build ResourceConfig from pod spec:\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 ResourceConfigForPod() \u2192 CPU shares, CFS quota, memory limit\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 PidsLimit if configured\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 MemoryQoS unified fields (memory.min, memory.high) if cgroup v2 + feature gate\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 cgroupManager.Create()\n```\n\nOn pod termination, pod workers call `PodContainerManager.Destroy()`:\n\n```\npodContainerManagerImpl.Destroy()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 tryKillingCgroupProcesses() \u2192 kill all PIDs in cgroup (up to 5 retries)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 cgroupManager.Destroy()    \u2192 rmdir the cgroup\n```\n\n### 3.5 Device Health Update Loop\n\nWhen a device plugin reports a device health change, the device manager sends to its internal `update` channel. A fan-in goroutine in `NewContainerManager` (`container_manager_linux.go:375`) forwards this to `cm.resourceUpdates`. The kubelet sync loop reads from `containerManager.Updates()` (`kubelet.go:2665`) and calls `handler.HandlePodSyncs()` for affected pods, causing a fresh status update that reflects the new device health.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n**Cgroup write failures on node allocatable enforcement**: `enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()` (`node_container_manager_linux.go:95`) spawns a background goroutine that retries `cgroupManager.Update()` indefinitely with 1-minute sleeps, emitting Kubernetes Warning events on each failure. This prevents a hard startup failure when existing pod memory usage temporarily exceeds the new limit.\n\n**QoS cgroup update failures**: `qosContainerManagerImpl.UpdateCgroups()` (`qos_container_manager_linux.go:316`) attempts a `retrySetMemoryReserve()` fallback that caps the limit to current memory usage when the first write is rejected. If updates still fail, the error is logged but the goroutine continues; QoS limits may drift from desired state until the next 1-minute reconcile.\n\n**CPU manager checkpoint corruption**: If `state.NewCheckpointState()` fails, the CPU manager refuses to start and the kubelet returns an error. The operator must drain the node and remove the state file. This is intentional\u2014silently starting with corrupt state would produce incorrect CPU pinning.\n\n**Device plugin crashes**: The device manager marks devices from a crashed plugin as unhealthy and sends updates via the health channel. Pods using those devices get re-synced; the kubelet emits events. The checkpoint retains allocations so that if the plugin reconnects before the pod is deleted, allocation state can be reconciled.\n\n**NUMA nodes > 8**: `topology_manager.go:41` defines `defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes = 8`. Exceeding this causes `topologymanager.NewManager()` to return an error, preventing kubelet startup with topology manager enabled on large multi-socket machines.\n\n**Swap enabled with `failSwapOn=true`**: `NewContainerManager` returns an error immediately, preventing kubelet from starting. With `failSwapOn=false`, the kubelet continues but emits a warning event about memory-backed volumes potentially being swapped to disk.\n\n**cgroup v1 on new kernels**: A deprecation warning (`CgroupV1DeprecatedWarning`) is defined in `container_manager.go:52`. cgroup v1 support is intended for removal in a future release.\n\n### 4.2 Design Tradeoffs\n\n**Two-phase admission/allocation**: The topology manager's `Admit()` phase calls `Allocate()` on hint providers before the container is created. This means device allocations are committed at pod admission time, not at container start time. If the container never starts (e.g., image pull failure), the device remains allocated until the kubelet cleans up the pod.\n\n**Checkpoint-based state persistence**: CPU, memory, and device managers all use checkpoint files under `KubeletRootDir`. This allows kubelet restarts without losing allocations. The downside is that checkpoint format changes require migration logic and draining.\n\n**Synchronous QoS hierarchy updates**: The QoS cgroup update goroutine holds a mutex for its entire update cycle. During that time, new pod admissions that need `UpdateQOSCgroups()` must wait. This is acceptable because the update is fast (a few cgroup writes) and happens only once per minute.\n\n**Noop implementations as a compile-time seam**: The `containerManagerStub` (`container_manager_stub.go`) and `podContainerManagerNoop` provide full no-op implementations of the interfaces. This decouples the kubelet's main path from the Linux-specific cgroup machinery at the cost of maintaining two parallel code paths.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customisation Hooks, and Risks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policy\n\n`cpumanager.Policy` is an interface (`policy.go`) with `Start()`, `Allocate()`, `RemoveContainer()`, `GetTopologyHints()`, `GetAllocatableCPUs()`. New policies can be registered by adding a `case` to the `switch` in `NewManager()`. Policy options (`CPUManagerPolicyOptions map[string]string` in `NodeConfig`) allow feature flags per policy without changing the interface.\n\nThe static policy has options including `full-pcpus-only` (require whole physical cores), `distribute-cpus-across-numa`, `distribute-cpus-across-cores`, and `align-by-socket`. These are parsed in `policy_options.go` and change the CPU assignment topology.\n\n**Risk**: A buggy policy can silently mis-assign CPUs or fail to clean up exclusive allocations; the CPU set leaked from a terminated container remains unavailable for new ones until the reconciler detects the container is gone.\n\n### 5.2 Topology Manager Policy and Scope\n\nBoth `TopologyManagerPolicy` and `TopologyManagerScope` are strings from `NodeConfig`. Adding a new policy requires adding a `policy_*.go` file and registering it in `topology_manager.go`. The scope (container vs. pod) changes whether hints are merged per-container or across all containers at once.\n\n**Risk**: `best-effort` silently allows non-optimal NUMA placement; operators may not notice increased cross-NUMA memory traffic until they measure latency. `restricted` and `single-numa-node` can cause admission failures that are opaque to end users if hint providers cannot agree.\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugins\n\nDevice plugins register via the plugin watcher (`GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()` returns a map including `DevicePlugin` \u2192 `deviceManager.GetWatcherHandler()`). Any DaemonSet can register additional resource types without modifying kubelet code. The device manager's `Allocate()` delegates entirely to the plugin's gRPC response.\n\n**Risk**: A device plugin that returns inconsistent topology information will cause the topology manager to make suboptimal NUMA placements. A plugin that crashes at `Allocate()` time causes pod admission to fail; kubelet will retry the admission on the next sync cycle.\n\n### 5.4 DRA Drivers\n\nDRA drivers register via the DRA plugin watcher (`DRAPlugin` key in `GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()`). The `dra.Manager` communicates with the driver to `PrepareResources()`, writing CDI device annotations that are passed to the CRI runtime. DRA is gated by `DynamicResourceAllocation` feature gate.\n\n**Risk**: DRA state is stored in `ResourceClaim` objects in the API server and locally in the DRA manager's state directory. Inconsistencies between these two sources of truth on kubelet restart require the `PodMightNeedToUnprepareResources()` / `UnprepareResources()` recovery path; if the driver itself is unavailable at unprepare time, resources may leak.\n\n### 5.5 MemoryQoS (cgroup v2 only)\n\nControlled by the `MemoryQoS` feature gate. When enabled, `memory.min` is set on QoS cgroups and pod cgroups to provide memory protection guarantees. The `Unified` map field in `ResourceConfig` carries arbitrary cgroup v2 key-value pairs, providing an extension point for future cgroup v2 features without changing the `ResourceConfig` struct.\n\n### 5.6 PodLevelResources\n\nThe `qos_container_manager_linux.go:188` references `kubefeatures.PodLevelResources` to decide whether to skip pod-level resource aggregation when computing Burstable CPU shares. This is an example of a feature gate that changes the aggregation semantics within an existing component.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance\n\n**CPU manager reconciliation**: The reconcile loop calls `UpdateContainerResources()` on the CRI runtime for every container whose CPU set has changed since the last reconcile. On a node with hundreds of containers and the static policy, this can produce bursts of gRPC calls. The reconcile period (`CPUManagerReconcilePeriod`, default 10 seconds) controls this tradeoff.\n\n**QoS cgroup update cost**: Every minute, `UpdateCgroups()` iterates all active pods to sum CPU requests. On nodes with many pods, this is O(pods \u00d7 containers). The update itself is a handful of cgroup writes, but the pod iteration under lock can delay admission.\n\n**Cgroup write latency on systemd**: When using the systemd cgroup driver, `cgroup_manager_linux.go` converts every cgroup name to a systemd slice path. Systemd must be notified via D-Bus for each cgroup operation. On high-density nodes this can become a bottleneck; the cgroupfs driver avoids this overhead.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability\n\n**Kubelet restart resilience**: CPU, memory, and device managers write state to checkpoint files before returning success from `Allocate()`. On restart, `Start()` reads the checkpoint and calls `UpdateContainerResources()` for any container still running to restore affinity. This means brief affinity drift (the container runs on the wrong CPUs) during the window between kubelet crash and restart recovery.\n\n**cgroup hierarchy divergence**: The QoS and pod container managers are responsible for creating and destroying cgroups in sync with pod lifecycle. If the kubelet crashes between creating a pod cgroup and launching the container, orphan cgroups may exist. `GetAllPodsFromCgroups()` on `podContainerManagerImpl` scans the filesystem to enumerate orphan pod cgroups, which `HandlePodCleanups()` uses for garbage collection.\n\n**`ShouldResetExtendedResourceCapacity()`**: Called on kubelet startup via `kubelet_resources.go`. The device manager returns `true` if the checkpoint indicates the node identity changed (e.g., node was recreated). In that case the kubelet zeroes extended resource capacity in the node status, forcing device plugins to re-register.\n\n### 6.3 Maintainability\n\n**cgroup v1 deprecation**: `container_manager.go:52` contains the deprecation warning. The v1-specific code paths in `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` and the v1 branches in `helpers_linux.go` represent ongoing maintenance burden. Removal requires coordinated changes across multiple files.\n\n**`klog.TODO()` debt**: Several methods in `container_manager_linux.go` (e.g., `PodHasExclusiveCPUs`, `GetCapacity`) call `klog.TODO()` because they lack a proper context. This is flagged in source comments as a known issue requiring refactoring to pass loggers through more of the call chain.\n\n**Mockery-generated mocks**: The `//go:generate mockery` directive in `container_manager.go` generates mocks for testing. The `.mockery.yaml` controls which interfaces are mocked. This keeps test doubles in sync with the interface, but any interface change requires running `go generate` and committing updated mock files.\n\n---\n\n## 7. File and Directory Map\n\n| Path | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` | `ContainerManager` interface, `NodeConfig`, `NodeAllocatableConfig`, helper functions |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` | Linux `containerManagerImpl`: construction, `Start()`, resource delegation |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` | Windows `containerManagerImpl`: capacity and device management only |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_stub.go` | No-op stub for tests and unsupported platforms |\n| `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` | # Kubelet Container Manager: Subsystem Architecture Guide

## 1. Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

### Purpose

The container manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm`) is the kubelet subsystem responsible for translating Kubernetes resource semantics—CPU requests, memory limits, QoS classes, device plugins, NUMA topology—into concrete OS-level enforcement. On Linux this means writing cgroup parameters. On other platforms it provides stubs or minimal implementations. It does not schedule pods (that is the kube-scheduler's job) nor does it launch containers (that is the CRI runtime's job). Its mandate is strictly _resource boundary enforcement_ and _device/hardware allocation_.

### Subsystem Boundaries

**Upstream inputs:**
- Pod specs from the kubelet's pod manager (via `ActivePodsFunc`)
- Node hardware topology from cAdvisor (`cadvisorapi.MachineInfo`)
- Feature gates from `utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate`
- CRI runtime service for reading current container state and updating container resources (`internalapi.RuntimeService`)
- Kubernetes API client for DRA (Dynamic Resource Allocation) claim resolution

**Downstream outputs:**
- Cgroup filesystem writes (memory limits, CPU shares/quotas, cpuset affinity, pids limits, hugetlb limits)
- `ContainerResources` updates sent to the CRI runtime via `UpdateContainerResources()`
- `RunContainerOptions` returned to `kuberuntime` containing device mounts, environment variables, and CDI device names
- A `resourceupdates.Update` channel consumed by the kubelet sync loop to re-sync pods whose device health changed

**Key external dependencies:**
- `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups` (runc libcontainer): the actual cgroup read/write operations
- `github.com/opencontainers/cgroups/systemd`: systemd cgroup name conversion
- cAdvisor for machine t
... (truncated)
